(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<introduction id="_b9c8648f-2535-0231-3dfe-665887a87dd4" obligation="informative">
<title id="_2b2e98d1-114a-3da4-8556-01ae0a724280">Introduction</title>
<p id="_e048e634-ddea-0f7a-aa6d-25b4b3c23e8c">The W3C Semantic Web Activity is defining a collection of technologies that enables a “web of data” where information is easily shared and reused across applications. Some key pieces of this technology stack are the RDF (Resource Description Framework) data model <eref type="inline" bibitemid="RDF" citeas="W3C rdf11-concepts"/>, <eref type="inline" bibitemid="RDFS" citeas="W3C rdf-schema"/>, the OWL Web Ontology Language <eref type="inline" bibitemid="OWL2" citeas="W3C owl2-overview"/> and the SPARQL protocol and RDF query language <eref type="inline" bibitemid="SPARQL" citeas="W3C sparql11-query"/>.</p>

<clause id="_03003783-b67c-06ae-2c3d-10623018e8cf" inline-header="false" obligation="informative">

000311term-RDFISO_4
term definition starts with article: RDF
<term id="_63354cb5-b90a-b440-3e1e-d0eb469452e3" anchor="term-RDF"> <preferred> <expression>
<name>RDF</name>
</expression>
</preferred>
<definition id="_3f230592-c17f-e905-35a6-9f553534c046"> <verbal-definition id="_19df912a-0691-6ccc-d741-4f274f6e924d"> <p id="_9b81a831-aa1b-6f1d-ab84-0818b46a067b">The Resource Description Framework (RDF) is a framework for representing information in the Web. RDF graphs are sets of subject-predicate-object triples, where the elements may be IRIs, blank nodes, or datatyped literals. They are used to express descriptions of resources. <eref type="inline" bibitemid="RDF" citeas="W3C rdf11-concepts"/> </p> </verbal-definition> </definition>

000321term-OWLISO_4
term definition starts with article: OWL
<term id="_1eb94a0e-8140-200d-8260-99734ccd8fe8" anchor="term-OWL"> <preferred> <expression>
<name>OWL</name>
</expression>
</preferred>
<definition id="_a2307d9e-87a9-4ec0-ee69-5738a2605d11"> <verbal-definition id="_b5b0ed1d-3546-7833-a83a-c75afe13dc5f"> <p id="_5f9ba324-34cb-c3a0-1cbc-d11e72d267f7">The OWL 2 Web Ontology Language, informally OWL 2, is an ontology language for the Semantic Web with formally defined meaning. OWL 2 ontologies provide classes, properties, individuals, and data values and are stored as Semantic Web documents. OWL 2 ontologies can be used along with information written in RDF, and OWL 2 ontologies themselves are primarily exchanged as RDF documents. <eref type="inline" bibitemid="OWL2" citeas="W3C owl2-overview"/> </p> </verbal-definition> </definition>

000363term-discrete-global-grid-systemISO_35
term definition ends with period: discrete global grid system
<term id="_317e3c57-f005-bc52-8668-4f1aeaa18114" anchor="term-discrete-global-grid-system"> <preferred> <expression>
<name>discrete global grid system</name>
</expression>
</preferred>
<definition id="_18f9ab88-e170-7e63-b50f-60f5a4366a70"> <verbal-definition id="_0e8d44a2-e236-d81a-84e9-1866dd9bb7b9"> <p id="_ab561744-f8b4-e961-0a46-b6258da2883b">A discrete global grid system (DGGS) is a spatial reference system that represents the Earth, or any other globe-like object, with a tessellation of nested cells. Generally, a DGGS will exhaustively partition the globe in closely packed hierarchical tessellations, each cell representing a homogenous value, with a unique identifier or indexing that allows for linear ordering, parent-child operations, and nearest neighbor algebraic operations.</p> </verbal-definition> </definition>
2

000368term-spatial-reference-systemISO_35
term definition ends with period: spatial reference system
<term id="_9ceef1ba-2a7d-6cf9-6a65-d90cf881e7e9" anchor="term-spatial-reference-system"> <preferred> <expression>

<definition id="_e512fcf1-9cb0-2e88-2a5d-9cb08462480e"> <verbal-definition id="_4911185d-0eb5-3abf-e7bb-f10816ad8074"> <p id="_f40acbb5-b0be-c7f6-95c4-56ac290d795b">A spatial reference system (SRS) is a system for establishing spatial position. A spatial reference system can use geographic identifiers (place names, for example), coordinates (in which case it is a coordinate reference system), or identifiers with structured geometry (in which case it is a discrete global grid system).</p> </verbal-definition> </definition>

000487_940a4331-e658-8c89-ed96-e35f0826b937STANDOC_48
(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_940a4331-e658-8c89-ed96-e35f0826b937" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_044942ca-9796-b4a6-70f4-4ab0218662d2">Core</title>
<p id="_9f13966d-cfec-aa95-2b44-8095f9f08718" anchor="core">This clause establishes the <strong>Core</strong> requirements class, with IRI <tt>/req/core</tt>, which has a single corresponding conformance class, <strong>Core</strong>, with IRI <tt>/conf/core</tt>. This requirements class defines a set of classes and properties for representing geospatial data. The resulting vocabulary — an ontology — can be used to construct SPARQL graph patterns for querying appropriately modeled geospatial data. The RDFS and OWL vocabularies have both been used so that the vocabulary can be understood by systems that support only RDFS entailment and by systems that support OWL-based reasoning.</p>

<p id="_f5d868f9-8ad7-a47d-8f57-8cef1e39809b">The figure below gives an overview of the classes and properties defined by GeoSPARQL in the <strong>Core</strong>, <strong>Topology Vocabulary Extension</strong> and <strong>Geometry Extension</strong>, <strong>Geometry Topology Extension</strong> and <strong>RDFS Entailment Extension</strong> Conformance Classes.</p>
2

<title id="_c7763598-7359-852b-5197-b7c4b0db205f">Classes</title>
<p id="_eaaec93e-fa17-ecd5-c273-7b6c2bf2dacf">Two main classes are defined: <xref target="class-spatialobject"> <display-text> <tt>Spatial Object</tt> </display-text> </xref> and <xref target="class-feature"> <display-text> <tt>Feature</tt> </display-text> </xref>. The class <xref target="class-feature"> <display-text> <tt>Feature</tt> </display-text> </xref> is equivalent to the UML class <tt>Feature</tt> defined in <eref type="inline" bibitemid="ISO19109" citeas="ISO 19109"/>.</p>

<p id="_83917dc9-d6a4-41bf-cfea-4706aa0083b8">Two container classes are defined: <xref target="class-spatialobjectcollection"> <display-text> <tt>SpatialObjectCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref> and <xref target="class-featurecollection"> <display-text> <tt>FeatureCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref>.</p>

000897_40a59eb4-25f6-c342-10a4-6d1feeaff850STANDOC_48
(generic warning) may contain ambiguous provision: For example, if a Feature my:f1 has two asserted default geometries, and those two geometries are disjoint polygons,​ the query below could return a non-zero count on a system supporting the GeoSPARQL Query Rewrite Extension (rule ).
<p id="_40a59eb4-25f6-c342-10a4-6d1feeaff850">GeoSPARQL does not restrict the cardinality of the <xref target="prop-hasdefaultgeometry"> <display-text>has default geometry</display-text> </xref> property. It is thus possible for a Feature to have more than one distinct default geometry or to have no default geometry. This situation does not result in a query processing error; SPARQL graph pattern matching simply proceeds as normal. Certain queries may, however, give logically inconsistent results. For example, if a Feature <tt>my:f1</tt> has two asserted default geometries, and those two geometries are disjoint polygons, the query below could return a non-zero count on a system supporting the GeoSPARQL Query Rewrite Extension (rule <link target="http://www.opengis.net/def/rule/geosparql/sfDisjoint"> <tt>geor:sfDisjoint</tt> </link>).</p>
2

(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_280d09a2-e5d0-6a2b-067b-63d36a3ad483" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_db081133-da17-edc9-31e0-d5bdebf8d99e">Topology Vocabulary Extension</title>
<p id="_70510c2e-fabf-e8dc-3410-f1d2925b2e64">This clause establishes the <em>Topology Vocabulary Extension</em> parameterized Requirements class. The IRI base is <tt>/req/topology-vocab-extension</tt>, which has a single corresponding Conformance Class <em>Topology Vocabulary Extension</em>, with IRI <tt>/conf/topology-vocab-extension</tt>. This Requirements class defines a vocabulary for asserting and querying topological relations between spatial objects. The class is parameterized so that different families of topological relations may be used, such as RCC8 and Egenhofer. These relations are generalized so that they may connect features as well as geometries.</p>

<requirement id="_457b499a-31c0-de9c-17aa-2789cc6799a6" model="default" type="requirements_class">
2



001204_5d05a35e-5081-ce57-0232-6cb63216df87STANDOC_48
(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_5d05a35e-5081-ce57-0232-6cb63216df87" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_6ade34e4-3b15-20fb-d7b9-5241e98e3aea">Geometry Extension</title>
<p id="_7e619836-69e6-3413-2b78-c4cf3db05520">This clause defines the <em>Geometry Extension</em> parameterized Requirements class with the base IRI <tt>/req/geometry-extension</tt>. There is a single corresponding conformance class <em>Geometry Extension</em>, with the IRI <tt>/conf/geometry-extension</tt>. These Requirements define a vocabulary for asserting and querying information about geometry data, and define query functions for operating on geometry data.</p>

<requirement id="_a77c0003-e237-1919-e4ad-97f0f4a31224" model="default" type="requirements_class">

001359_297ddf49-f5c6-c34e-c620-3d01ed42eefdSTANDOC_48
(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_297ddf49-f5c6-c34e-c620-3d01ed42eefd" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_eb5cae13-a53d-f0df-aad2-570e68f4d863">Geometry Class</title>
<p id="_9e12f70f-9173-3160-6588-ae5a7d621de7">A single root geometry class is defined: <xref target="class-geometry"> <display-text> <tt>Geometry</tt> </display-text> </xref>. In addition, properties are defined for describing geometry data and for associating geometries with features.</p>

<p id="_44f1cd15-4cef-a3d0-438a-c7be9d78e3d3">One container class is defined: <xref target="class-geometrycollection"> <display-text> <tt>GeometryCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref>.</p>
2



001406_fce204d7-d3fe-ef01-3db2-57cb449fa8d5STANDOC_48
(generic warning) Note may contain permission: This class contains whole Geometry instances, which may have more information within them than just a geometry serialization
<note id="_fce204d7-d3fe-ef01-3db2-57cb449fa8d5"> <p id="_fb641a0a-4d77-8444-0b37-ab8875ff9666">There is no RDF/ontology relationship between this <xref target="class-geometrycollection"> <display-text> <tt>GeometryCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref> class and the Simple Features Vocabulary’s <link target="http://www.opengis.net/ont/sf#GeometryCollection"> <tt>sf:GeometryCollection</tt> </link> class since the former is a collection of <tt>Geometry</tt> objects and the latter is to be used for compound geometry literals.</p>

<p id="_2ed97699-2155-2f39-2a5c-878c50b76c92"> <link target="http://www.opengis.net/ont/sf#GeometryCollection"> <tt>sf:GeometryCollection</tt> </link> instances can act as input or output of GeoSPARQL functions whereas <xref target="class-geometrycollection"> <display-text> <tt>GeometryCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref> instances are more likely to be used for grouping <tt>Geometry</tt> objects for other purposes.</p>

<p id="_f24a2876-17b0-2167-b26f-3aa39946ddbd">Many geometry literal formats also have the ability to represent multiple geometries. Both the OGC Geography Markup Language (GML) and KML use a <em>MultiGeometry</em> type and Well Known Text (WKT) and GeoJSON use a <em>GeometryCollection</em> type. While the names of some of these objects are the same as this class’ and all the concepts are similar, there is also no RDF/ontology relationship between this class and these literals. This class contains whole <tt>Geometry</tt> instances, which may have more information within them than just a geometry serialization.</p>
2

(generic warning) Note may contain requirement: There is no RDF/​ontology relationship between this GeometryCollection class and the Simple Features Vocabulary’s class since the former is a collection of Geometry objects and the latter is to be used for compound geometry literals

002558geometry_​topology_​extensionSTANDOC_48

<title id="_7356648c-1010-0e2d-2434-a2c999e102de">Geometry Topology Extension</title>
<p id="_bc21eadc-c45c-e278-a814-00ae46895c3b">This clause establishes the <em>Geometry Topology Extension</em> parameterized Requirements class with base IRI <tt>/req/geometry-topology-extension</tt>, which defines a collection of topological query functions that operate on geometry literals. These Requirements have a single corresponding conformance class <em>Geometry Topology Extension</em>, with IRI <tt>/conf/geometry-topology-extension</tt>.</p>

Each query function is associated with a defining DE-9IM intersection pattern. Possible pattern values are:</p>

002776_ef26fe28-13b1-dbf3-f010-0782b90a6915ISO_43
subclause is only child
<clause id="_ef26fe28-13b1-dbf3-f010-0782b90a6915" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_73636e0a-9434-fddb-b929-3e27d66e7ffe">Geometry Class Hierarchy</title>
<p id="_2805f458-50e5-4bb7-9d2c-df9a9c4fd50e">The Simple Features specification presents a geometry class hierarchy. It is straightforward to represent this class hierarchy in RDFS and OWL by constructing IRIs for geometry classes using the following pattern: <tt>http://www.opengis.net/ont/sf#{geometry class}</tt> and by asserting appropriate <link target="http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf"> <tt>rdfs:subClassOf</tt> </link> statements. The <em>Simple Features Vocabulary</em> resource within GeoSPARQL 1.1 (sibling resource to this specification) does this. The following list gives the class hierarchy with each indented item being a subclass of the item in the line above. The class hierarchy starts with GeoSPARQL’s <tt>Geometry</tt> class of which <link target="http://www.opengis.net/ont/sf#Geometry"> <tt>sf:Geometry</tt> </link> is a subclass:</p>

<sourcecode id="_a3d947db-7451-d605-7a4b-e8d4cd4d31e0" lang="turtle" unnumbered="true"> <body>geo:Geometry
2



002820rdfse_gmlSTANDOC_48
(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_d1c41ac4-45e4-ea7e-b63c-78b82add5647" anchor="rdfse_gml" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_a9b1f83a-7b14-619a-1d11-97f73122533c">GML Serialization</title>
<p id="_35a15b2a-82b9-862f-0e15-3f2d2c8d249a">This section establishes Requirements for representing geometry data in RDF based on GML as defined by Geography Markup Language Encoding Standard <eref type="inline" bibitemid="OGC07-036" citeas="OGC 07-036"/>.</p>

<clause id="_4eafae9a-d7a4-72a7-b55b-2f296f40c4dc" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
2



002824_4eafae9a-d7a4-72a7-b55b-2f296f40c4dcISO_43
subclause is only child
<clause id="_4eafae9a-d7a4-72a7-b55b-2f296f40c4dc" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_5a56e21a-2e77-628d-24ed-6a34b8561ef5">Geometry Class Hierarchy</title>
<p id="_ebdd927b-1f90-5352-e3e9-330f430aff53">An RDF/OWL class hierarchy can be generated from the GML schema that implements <tt>GM_Object</tt> by constructing IRIs for geometry classes using the following pattern: <tt>http://www.opengis.net/ont/gml#{GML Element}</tt> and by asserting appropriate <link target="http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf"> <tt>rdfs:subClassOf</tt> </link> statements.</p>

<p id="_c78b5bd9-0bfc-8cd6-bd78-072bb57a2b7e">The example RDF snippet below encodes the Polygon class from GML 3.2.</p>

002847_db46a735-9259-2c52-c430-982a2fdfff2cSTANDOC_48
(generic warning) Hanging paragraph in clause
<clause id="_db46a735-9259-2c52-c430-982a2fdfff2c" inline-header="false" obligation="normative">
<title id="_f9e3b3a4-ecb7-8e25-c06d-aa55cbae52f2">Query Rewrite Extension</title>
<p id="_88777423-b639-61e6-82ab-2a621df7d4aa">This clause establishes the <em>Query Rewrite Extension</em> parameterized Requirements class with base IRI <tt>/req/query-rewrite-extension</tt>, which has a single corresponding conformance class <em>Query Rewrite Extension</em>, with IRI <tt>/conf/query-rewrite-extension</tt>. These Requirements define a set of RIF rules <eref type="inline" bibitemid="RIF" citeas="W3C rif-overview"/> that use topological extension functions defined in <xref target="Geometry Extension"/> to establish the existence of direct topological predicates defined in <xref target="Topology Vocabulary Extension"/>. One possible implementation strategy is to transform a given query by expanding a triple pattern involving a direct spatial predicate into a series of triple patterns and an invocation of the corresponding extension function as specified in the RIF rule.</p>

<requirement id="_98a38c01-e461-ea4f-6c6b-43e094258a2b" model="default" type="requirements_class">
2



002904_cd49c76e-8b7a-d648-9dbc-f4669493a22cSTANDOC_48
(generic warning) All lists must be preceded by colon or full stop: Parameters
<ul id="_cd49c76e-8b7a-d648-9dbc-f4669493a22c"> <li> <p id="_f673412f-6e87-4ec3-7615-28ab7831397f"> <strong>relation_family</strong>: Specifies the set of topological spatial relations to support.</p>
</li>
<li> <p id="_50a14c81-e5c5-799c-6624-97c9b144130a"> <strong>serialization</strong>: Specifies the serialization standard to use for geometry literals.</p>
</li>
<li> <p id="_7199a234-3062-a915-d0b4-d43408c37546"> <strong>version</strong>: Specifies the version of the serialization format used.</p>

<p id="_9355566f-650e-7c81-165e-8b4c303801b5">When using a query transformation strategy, this triple pattern could invoke none of the GeoSPARQL rules or all of the rules. Implementations are free to support either of these alternatives.</p>

004290_336a9dfe-4522-2729-e177-f6dd41495ed8STANDOC_48
(generic warning) may contain ambiguous provision: There are several GeoSPARQL properties that suggest they could be used with particular Simple Features Vocabulary geometry types, for instance,​ has­Centroid indicates is could be used with a and has­BoundingBox indicates use with an sf:​Envelope.
<p id="_336a9dfe-4522-2729-e177-f6dd41495ed8">There are several GeoSPARQL properties that suggest they could be used with particular <em>Simple Features Vocabulary</em> geometry types, for instance, <xref target="prop-hascentroid"> <display-text> <tt>hasCentroid</tt> </display-text> </xref> indicates is could be used with a <link target="http://www.opengis.net/ont/sf#Point"> <tt>sf:Point</tt> </link> and <xref target="prop-hasboundingbox"> <display-text> <tt>hasBoundingBox</tt> </display-text> </xref> indicates use with an <tt>sf:Envelope</tt>.</p>

<p id="_d24d14ac-15e4-64b1-aeb4-ab53c01959cc">a future version of GeoSPARQL that handled spatio-temporal Features could perhaps claim that <xref target="class-feature"> <display-text> <tt>Feature</tt> </display-text> </xref> is a <link target="http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf"> <tt>rdfs:subClassOf</tt> </link> <link target="http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/BFO_0000011"> <tt>obo:BFO_0000011</tt> </link> “spatiotemporal region”, however inconsistencies from this mapping will occur due to the current Feature/”spatial region” mapping above and this will need to be handled</p>

<title id="_e810a36f-6a97-d764-646a-078f233784bf">CQL / GeoSPARQL Mapping</title>
<clause id="_3d1a0196-e18d-4f50-6257-805667b41573" inline-header="false" obligation="informative">
<title id="_c7ed2e94-3638-71f5-5cb1-1ac34dc53bab">F.0. Overview</title>
<p id="_63b15632-8b8e-ba65-45de-8a042414dae1">This annex presents a mapping between the Common Query Language(CQL) <eref type="inline" bibitemid="CQLDEF" citeas="OGC 19-079r1"/> and GeoSPARQL as well as generic SPARQL <eref type="inline" bibitemid="SPARQL" citeas="W3C sparql11-query"/>. This is likely of relevance to the delivery of GeoSPARQL data via systems such as the OGC’s Web Feature Service <eref type="inline" bibitemid="WFS" citeas="ISO 19142"/> and OGC API Features <eref type="inline" bibitemid="OGCAPIF" citeas="OGC 17-069r4"/> which implement CQL.</p>
1



005939_74283e55-a408-a11a-b141-5040f82831b6STANDOC_48
(generic warning) Note may contain permission: There is no such restriction in GeoSPARQL: Features may be members of one or more Feature Collections
<note id="_74283e55-a408-a11a-b141-5040f82831b6"> <p id="_7df5557e-6d73-46d7-ff30-04f54b0cef49">Some CQL-implementing systems, such as OGC API, have fixed notions of Feature Collections and require that Features be members of exactly one Feature Collection. There is no such restriction in GeoSPARQL: Features may be members of one or more Feature Collections.</p>
</note>
2



005959_3cd70cc5-b983-d5ab-cdbb-3cfea7628f39STANDOC_48

If the back-end data store also contains information for the <xref target="class-featurecollection"> <display-text> <tt>FeatureCollection</tt> </display-text> </xref> instance then this may be queried for. If not, the API might need to create such data</p>

006774OGC07-036ISO_42
non-ISO/IEC reference is allowed as normative only subject to the conditions in ISO/IEC DIR 2 10.2: 
  2026-01-09
  
OpenGIS Geography Markup Language (GML) Encoding Standard

  
OpenGIS Geography Markup Language (GML) Encoding Standard

  https://portal.ogc.org/files/?artifact_id=20509
  07-036
  
    2007-10-05
  
  
    
    
      
          Clemens Portele       

    
  
  
    
    
      
Open Geospatial Consortium

    
  
  en
  Latn
  The OpenGIS® Geography Markup Language Encoding Standard (GML) The Geography Markup Language (GML) is an XML grammar for expressing geographical features. GML serves as a modeling language for geographic systems as well as an open interchange format for geographic transactions on the Internet. As with most XML based grammars, there are two parts to the grammar – the schema that describes the document and the instance document that contains the actual data.
A GML document is described using a GML Schema. This allows users and developers to describe generic geographic data sets that contain points, lines and polygons. However, the developers of GML envision communities working to define community-specific application schemas [en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GML_Application_Schemas] that are specialized extensions of GML. Using application schemas, users can refer to roads, highways, and bridges instead of points, lines and polygons. If everyone in a community agrees to use the same schemas they can exchange data easily and be sure that a road is still a road when they view it.

Clients and servers with interfaces that implement the OpenGIS® Web Feature Service Interface Standard[http://www.opengeospatial.org/standards/wfs] read and write GML data. GML is also an ISO standard (ISO 19136:2007) [www.iso.org/iso/iso_catalogue/catalogue_tc/catalogue_detail.htm?csnumber=32554 ].  
See also the GML pages on OGC Network: http://www.ogcnetwork.net/gml .
